тАШ рдЙрд╖рд╛ рдЙрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреА ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреИрд░реНрдШрддрдорд╕рдГ рдХрдХреНрд╖реАрд╡рдд рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореБрд╖рд╕реНрдпрдореН ред тАШ рдЙрд╖рд╛ рдЙрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреА ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрд╕реНрддреБ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рдПрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

124
Dawn
Kakс╣г─лvant Dairghatamasa
13 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Another virtuosic Dawn hymn. Here the poet takes the usual generic themes, espe cially Dawn as a beautiful woman, and creates highly specific images, especially in verses 7тАУ8, which provide a series of almost sociological portraits of ancient Indian female figures. In verse 7 we first (p─Бda a) meet a brotherless girl boldly approaching men; since the brother was important in finding and arranging suitable matches, a brotherless girl was at a disadvantage in the marriage market and needed to take initiative on her own. (See Schmidt 1987: 30тАУ75.) The next image is a pun (p─Бda b), with one harmless generic image and one shockingly specific one. In the harmless reading a figure, presumably male, mounts a chariot to seek prizes; in the other a woman, presumably a prostitute, shows herself off on a platform for money. The third image (p─Бdas cd) is of the legitimate wife adorned for her husband, but even there the image shades into that of a loose woman showing her breast. The next verse (8) treats the common theme of the sisters Dawn and Night, but again Dawn is presented in a particular female role. In the second p─Бda, the тАЬgirl to be gazed uponтАЭ may well refer to the display motif of the ancient Indian self-choice marriage (Svayaс╣Гvara; see Jamison 2001), while the тАЬmaidens with a choiceтАЭ may refer to the same phenomena, girls making their choice of bridegroom at a specially called assembly (see Jamison 2003).
Even more striking perhaps is verse 4, where Dawn is compared to three differ ent animals or their parts: she is glossy like the breast of a waterbird who preens it;

she reveals herself like an elephant kneeling to drink; and she wakens the sleeping like a fly, buzzing around again and again. (We owe these interpretations to Thieme 1965 [=1971: 214тАУ27].)
Nothing in the rest of the hymn is quite so quirky, but the standard tropes are well handled. The common counterpoint between individual Dawn and the multi tude of identical dawns that have preceded and will follow todayтАЩs dawn is found in verses 2тАУ3, 6, and 9. Another common theme, the diversity of beings that Dawn awakens, appears in verses 1, 6, and 12. The final verses of the hymn raise the hope of gifts and rewards that will come with the dawn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the (sacred) fire is kindled, Uс╣г─Б sheds abundant light, dispersing (the darkness) like the rising sun; may the divine Savit─Бbestow upon usfor our use, wealth of both bipeds and quadrupeds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

For our use: ityatai, lit. = for going; i.e. for carrying on our own affairs

Jamison Brereton

Dawn as she dawns when the fire is being kindled; the sun as it risesтАФ each has propped up its own light widely.
God Savitar here and now has impelled forth our two-footed, forth our four-footed, each to go to its task.

Griffith

THE Dawn refulgent when the fire is kindled, and the Sun rising, far diffuse their brightness.
Savitar, God, hath sent us forth to labour, each quadruped, each biped, to be active.

Geldner

W├дhrend das Feuer angez├╝ndet wird, hat die aufleuchtende Usas, hat der aufgehende Surya sein Licht weithin aufgesteckt. Gott Savitri hat unsere Zwei- und Vierf├╝├Яler nunmehr angetrieben, an ihr Gesch├дft zu gehen.

Grassmann

Die Uschas leuchtend bei entflammtem Feuer, die Sonn’ im Aufgehn, breitet weit ihr Licht aus; Gott Savitar hat uns erweckt zur Arbeit, und Mensch und Thier, was F├╝sse hat, zum Gehen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUnimpeding divine rites, although wearing away the ages of mankind, the dawn shines the similitude of the (mornings) that have passed, or that are to be forever, the first of those that are to come.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Unimpeding: aminati ahiс╣Гsant─л, not injuring, not opposing, not unsuited to; being the fit season for performance

Jamison Brereton

Not belittling the divine commandments, but diminishing human (life-) spans,
the last of those who, one by one, have gone, the first of those who come hitherтАФDawn has flashed forth. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

├бminat─л (2a) and n├б тАж min─Бti (3d)(cf. also n├б min─Бti I.123.9) receive different tr. here both because they have different objects and because ├бminat─л is contrastively paired with praminat─л╠Б(2b).

Griffith

Not interrupting heavenly ordinances, although she minisheth human generations.
The last of endless morns that have departed, the first of those that come, Dawn brightly shineth.

Geldner

Ohne die g├╢ttlichen Gebote zu schm├дlern, aber die menschlichen Lebenszeiten schm├дlernd, ist Usas aufgeleuchtet als die letzte der vielen Vergangenen, als die erste der kommenden.

Verk├╝rzend nie die Ordnungen der G├╢tter, doch k├╝rzend stets der Menschen Lebensalter, Als letzte der vergangnen und als erste der kommenden erstrahlt die Morgenr├╢the.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShe, the daughter of heaven, is beheld in the east, gracious and arrayed in light; she travels steadily along the path of the sun, as if cognizant (of his plural asure), and damages not the quarters (of the horizon).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This Daughter of Heaven has appeared opposite, dressed in light, in the same way (as the others), from the east.
She follows along the path of truth, straight to the goal. Like one who knows the way, she does not confound the directions. с│У

├бminat─л (2a) and n├б тАж min─Бti (3d)(cf. also n├б min─Бti I.123.9) receive different tr. here both because they have different objects and because ├бminat─л is contrastively paired with praminat─л╠Б(2b).

Griffith

There in the eastern region she, Heaven’s Daughter, arrayed in garments all of light, appeareth.
Truly she followeth the path of Order, nor faileth, knowing well, the heavenly quarters.

Geldner

Dort ist die Tochter des Himmels in Licht gekleidet ein wie alle Male im Ost erschienen. Sie wandelt richtig den Weg des Gesetzes; wie eine Wegkundige verfehlt sie nicht die Richtungen.

Grassmann

Es l├дsst sich blicken diese Himmelstochter im Osten, ganz in Lichtgewand gekleidet, Sie schreitet stracks entlang den Pfad der Ordnung, des Wegs bewusst verfehlt sie nicht die Richtung.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShe is beheld nigh at hand, (radiant) as the breast of the illuminator (the sun); and, like Nodhas, has made manifest many plural asing (objects); like a matron she awakens (her) sleeping (children), and of all (feminine les who are) stirring betimes, she, the most unvarying, repeatedly appears.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъundhyuvo na vakс╣гas: ┼Ыundhyu = sun, the collective solar rays;

┼Ъundhyu = a water-bird of white colour; the morning light is compared to its white plural mage;

┼Ъundhyuvaс╕е = plural waters (Nirukta 4.16); Nodhas, the с╣Ыс╣гi, displays his wishes by his prayers and praises, so the dawn puts forth the light that is accessible to all the world;

Admasad: adma, food or a dwelling; sad, who abides; the mistress of the house, or one who has to cook the food of her family; she rises with the dawn and wakes up the sleepers of the household

Jamison Brereton

She has appeared like the breast of a preening waterbird. Like a female elephant she has revealed her intimate parts.
Wakening the sleeping like a fly, she has come as the latest of those who, one by one, have come here again (and again).

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. follows that of Thieme (KZ 79 [1965] – KlSch 214-27), cited also in the published introduction.; for doubts, esp. about the interpr. of p─Бda b, see Scarlatta 272-73.

Griffith

Near is she seen, as ’twere the Bright One’s bosom: she showeth sweet things like a new song-singer.
She cometh like a fly awaking sleepers, of all returning dames most true and constant.

Geldner

Es zeigt sich ihre Brust wie die eines Sundhyvogels, wie Nodhas hat sie ihre lieben Sachen enth├╝llt. Wie eine Fliege weckt sie die Schlafenden; als erste unter den vielen Wiedergekehrten ist sie gekommen.

Grassmann

Ihr Busen zeigt sich wie der reinen Jungfrau, als zarte Maid enth├╝llt sie ihre Reize; Als Tischgenossin weckte sie die Schl├дfer, als j├╝ngste kam sie der sich stets erneu’nden.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBorn in the eastern quarter of the spacious firmament, she displays a banner of rays of light. plural ced on the lap of both parents (heaven and earth), filling them (with radiance), she enjoys vast and wide-spread renown.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In the eastern half of the dusky realm that cannot be flown to, the begetter of cows has put forth her beacon.
She spreads out further, more widely, filling both laps of her two parents [=Heaven and Earth].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax apty├б- is connected by Grassmann, Oldenberg, and, tentatively, EWA (s.v. ├бnapta-) with тАШwaterтАЩ. Geldner leaves it untr.; Witzel Got┼Н as тАШ├дussereтАЩ without comment. I follow RenouтАЩs tentative suggestion тАШinaccessible au volтАЩ (to тИЪpat), with perhaps more enthusiasm than he shows for it.

Griffith

There in the east half of the watery region the Mother of the Cows hath shown her ensign.
Wider and wider still she spreadeth onward, and filleth full the laps of both heir Parents.

An der ├╢stlichen Seite des …….Raumes hat die Mutter der K├╝he ihr Banner aufgesteckt. Sie breitet sich immer weiter in die Breite aus, bis sie den Scho├Я beider Eltern ausf├╝llt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVerily she, the wide-expanded Uс╣г─Б, neglects not (to give) the joy of sight to those of her own or of a different nature; visible in her faultless person n, and brightly shining, she passes not by the littleror the great.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Aj─Бmim na parivс╣Ыс╣Зakti j─Бmim: j─Бmi = saj─Бt─лya, of the same species, i.e. of divine beings, the gods;

Aj─Бmi = notof the same species; vij─Бt─лya, mankind; she passes not by: she lights up all things, from an atom to a mountain

Jamison Brereton

Just thus is she, the latest of many, to be seen. Neither the non-kin does she avoid, nor the kin.
Exulting in her spotless body, neither from the small does she retreat, nor from the great, as she shines forth.

Griffith

She, verily, exceeding vast to look on debarreth from her light nor kin nor stranger.
Proud of her spotless form she, brightly shining, turneth not from the high nor from the humble.

Geldner

Also gibt sich diese als die erste unter vielen zum Beschauen; sie geht nicht dem Fremden noch dem Verwandten aus dem Wege. Stolz auf ihren makellosen Leib zieht sie sich nicht vor Klein und Gro├Я zur├╝ck, wenn sie erstrahlt.

Grassmann

Die herrliche entzieht sich nicht dem Anblick, nicht der verwandten, noch der unverwandten, In makelloser Sch├╢nheit herrlich prangend verbirgt ihr Licht sie hohen nicht, noch niedern.

Elizarenkova

рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShe goes to the west, as (a woman who has) no brother (repairs) to her male (relatives); and like one ascending the hall (of justice) for the recovery of property, (she mounts in the sky to claim her lustre); and like a wife desirous to plural ase her husband, Uс╣г─Б puts on becoming attire, and smiling as it were, displays her charms.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abhr─Бteva puс╣Гsa eti prat─лc─л = as a damsel who has no brother, averted from her own abiding plural ce (garta iti gс╣Ыhan─Бma, kс╣Ыdaro gartaс╕е (Nirukta 3.4.3), goes to or relies upon her male relatives, puс╣Гsaс╕е, for support; or it may mean that she is in such case to offer the funeral cakes to her progenitors; prat─лc─л, with face averted, as applicable to Uс╣г─Б, means looking or going to the west; gart─Бrug iva sanaye dhan─Бn─Бm, like one who ascends (─Бruс╕е, to mount) a house (garta-gс╣Ыha) for the gift or receipt of riches;

Garta = stool or table on which dice are thrown; there is a practice in the south, in which a childless widow seeks to obtain support from her husband’s relatives by repairing to a gambling-house; cf. Muller, Preface, 2nd vol. of the с╣Ъgveda,p. xvi

Jamison Brereton

Like a brotherless (girl) she goes right up to menтАФlike one mounting a chariot seat to win prizes [/(display-)platform to gain property].
Like an eager wife, richly dressed, for her husband, Dawn, like a wanton, lets her breast spill over.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the female figures here, see published introduction. Though most interpr. (see recently Scarlatta [463], Witzel Got┼Н) see only a male figure in the simile in b (a charioteer seeking prizes), I find it unlikely that the middle simile of three, the two outer of which depict striking female types, would compare Dawn only to a male. As indicated in the published introduction, I think it is a double entendre, with not only the prizeseeking male competitor on his chariot seat but also a prostitute displaying herself on a platform or stage for money (or whatever counted for money in that period).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sister (night) has prepared a birth-plural ce for her elder sister (day), and having amde it known to her, departs. Uс╣г─Б, dispersing the darkness with the rays of the sun, illumines the world, like congregated lightnings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The (one) sister has left the natal place to her older sister. She goes away from her, like (a girl) to be gazed upon.
Dawning forth with the rays of the sun, she smears unguent on herself, like (maidens) with a choice going to assemblies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, I believe that this verse continues the series of female portraits, this time with two vignettes of the svayaс╣Гvara (тАШself-choiceтАЩ) marriage.

On the basis of I.113.1, Geldner suggests persuasively that the subj. of p─Бda a is Night and her older sister is Dawn. Nonetheless, I take the subj. of b to be Dawn, who is going away from Night. The crucial word in b is pratic├бkс╣гy─Г/─Б (latter Pp.), which can be either a gerund (-─Г) or a gerundive (-─Б). Most (though not Oldenberg) take it as the latter, as I do, but with the sense тАЬto be seen againтАЭ (e.g., Geldner тАЬdie man wiedersehen sollтАЭ), that is, as one who will return. But this is not the standard meaning of pr├бti тИЪcakс╣г, which simply means тАШgaze uponтАЩ. Here I think тАЬto be gazed uponтАЭ represents the display motif of the svayaс╣Гvara marriage: before the girl exercises her choice among the assembled suitors, she enters the arena (vel sim.) and is announced and displayed for all to see (for disc. see esp. Jamison 1999 [Penelope] and for this passage in general Jamison 2003 [Fs. H.-P. Schmidt], pp. 42-44).

The choosing maidens (vr─Б╠Бс╕е) of the same marriage type are the topic of p─Бda d.

suv─Б╠Б┼Ы─Б(с╕е) in 7c is neatly echoed by sv├бs─Б opening 8a.

Griffith

The Sister quitteth, for the elder Sister, her place, and having looked on her departeth.
She decks her beauty, shining forth with sunbeams, like women trooping to the festal meeting.

Geldner

Die Schwester hat der ├дlteren Schwester den Platz ger├дumt; sie geht von ihr wie eine, die man wiedersehen soll. Mit den Strahlen des Surya aufleuchtend legt sie sich Schminke auf wie Lockm├дdchen, die zum Feste gehen.

Grassmann

Die Schwester r├дumt der edleren den Sitz ein, und geht davon, sobald sie sie gewahr wird, Und Uschas, leuchtend mit der Sonne Strahlen, schm├╝ckt sich mit Schmuck, wie Scharen die zum Fest gehn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOf all these sisters who have gone before, a successor daily follows the one that has preceded. So may new dawns, like the old, bringing fortunate days, shine upon us blessed with affluence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Day after day the latest of those earlier sisters advances from behind toward the earlier one.
Let the newer ones now dawn richly for us as of oldтАФthe
day-bright dawns.

Griffith

To all these Sisters who ere now have vanished a later one each day in course succeedeth.
So, like the past, with days of happy fortune, may the new Dawns shine forth on us with riches.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAwaken, wealth-abounding, Uс╣г─Б, those whose delight (in holy offerings); let the (niggard) traders, reluctant wake (for such a purpose), sleep on. Arise, opulent Uс╣г─Б, bearing wealth to the liberal (worshipper); speaker of truth, who are the waster away (of living creatures), arise, bearing wealth to him who praises you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Awaken those who grant, bounteous Dawn; unawakening let the niggards sleep.
Richly dawn for the bounteous ones, o bounteous one, richly for the praiser, o liberal-spirited one, as you rouse them.

Griffith

Rouse up, O Wealthy One, the liberal givers; let niggard traffickers sleep on unwakened:
Shine richly, Wealthy One, on those who worship, richly, glad.
Dawn while wasting, on the singer.

Geldner

Erwecke, freigebige Usas, die Spender; ohne zu erwachen sollen die Knauser schlafen. Leucht reiches Gut den freigebigen Herren zu, du Freigebige, reiches Gut dem Lobs├дnger zu, du Gro├Яm├╝tige, die du wach machst!

Grassmann

Erweck die Spender, reiche Morgenr├╢the, die Geiz’gen m├╢gen schlafen ohn’ Erwachen, Mit Reichthum strahle, reiche du, den F├╝rsten, mit Gut dem S├дnger, edle, ihn erlabend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis youthful Uс╣г─Б, approached from the east; she harnesses her team of purple oxen. Assuredly she will disperse the darkness, a manifest sign (of day) in the firmament; the (sacred) fire is kindled in every dwelling.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This young woman has whitened down from the east. She yokes the forefront of the ruddy cows.
She will dawn forth now; her beacon will stand out. Agni will reverently come to house after house.

Griffith

This young Maid from the east hath shone upon us; she harnesseth her team of bright red oxen.
She will beam forth, the light will hasten hither, and Agni will be present in each dwelling.

Geldner

Im Osten schimmerte die junge Frau hernieder, sie schirrt die Reihe ihrer roten Rinder an. Jetzt m├╢ge sie aufleuchten; ihr Banner soll vorausgehen: In jedem Hause stellt sich das Feuer ein.

Grassmann

Von Osten her ergl├дnzte diese Jungfrau, sie schirrt sich an die Schar der rothen Rinder; sie strahle nun, und vorw├дrts dring’ ihr Lichtschein, und Feuer stell sich ein in jedem Hause.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAt your dawning, (Uс╣г─Б), the various birds rise up from their nests, and men who have to earn their bread (quit their homes). You bring, divine (Uс╣г─Б), much wealth to the liberal mortal who is present in the chamber (of sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nara┼Ыca pitubh─Бjaс╕е-ann─Бrthinaс╕е, seeking for food

Jamison Brereton

The birds have also flown up from their dwelling and the men who partake of food, at your first flush.
To the one who is at home you convey much of value, goddess Dawn, and to the pious mortal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬone being at homeтАЭ (am─Б╠Бs├бnt-) may contrast implicitly with the тАЬEarly-comingтАЭ one (pr─Бtar├нtvan-) who forms the subject of the 1st half of the next hymn (I.125). In that hymn the Pr─Бtaritvan engages in dialogue with a person who is probably a householder, that is, in the words of our verse, one being at home.

This vs. is identical to VI.64.6; for further comm. see there.

Griffith

As the birds fly forth from their resting places, so men with store of food rise at thy dawning.
Yea, to the liberal mortal who remaineth at home, O Goddess Dawn, much good thou bringest.

Geldner

Selbst die V├╢gel sind bei deinem Aufleuchten aus dem Neste aufgeflogen und die M├дnner, die ihre Nahrung zu sich nehmen, von dem Lager. Dem daheim Bleibenden bringst du viel Gutes, G├╢ttin Usas, dem opferspendenden Sterblichen.

Grassmann

Bei deinem Leuchten fliegen auf die V├╢gel aus ihrem Nest, die M├дnner suchen Nahrung: dem, der daheim ist, f├╝hrst du vieles Gut zu, dem frommen Mann, G├╢ttin Morgenr├╢the.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬPraiseworthy Uс╣г─Бs, be glorified by this (my hymn); graciously disposed towards us, augment (our prosperity); and may we obtain, goddesses, through your favour, wealth; a hundred and a thousand fold.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You have been praised, praiseworthy ones, by my sacred formulation. You, eager (for it), have been strengthened, o Dawns.
Goddesses, with your help may we win spoils in hundreds and
thousands.

Griffith

Praised through my prayer be ye who should be lauded. Ye have increased our wealth, ye Dawns who love us.
Goddesses, may we win by your good favour wealth to be told by hundreds and by thousands.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЙрд╖рд╛рд╕ рдЙрд╖реЛрднрд┐рд╕реНрддреБрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд╕реНрддреЛрдореНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрд╡реАрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛ рдЙрд╢рддреАрд░реНрдпреВрдпрдВ рдореЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрддреЛрдвреНрд╡рдорд╡реАрд╡реГрдзрдзреНрд╡рдореНред рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдорд╡рд╕рд╛ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд┐рдгрдВ рдЪ рд╢рддрд┐рдирдВ рдЪ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдВ рд╕рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╕рд░рд╣рд╕реНрдпрд╡реЗрджрд╛рджрд┐рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдмреЛрдзрдВ рд╕рдиреЗрдо рее резрей рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╕реНрддреЛрдвреНрд╡рдореН) рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдд (рд╕реНрддреЛрдореНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рд╛рдГ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛) рд╡реЗрджреЗрди (рдореЗ) рдорд╣реНрдпрдореН (рдЕрд╡реАрд╡реГрдзрдзреНрд╡рдореН) рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдд (рдЙрд╢рддреАрдГ) рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ (рдЙрд╖рд╛рд╕рдГ) рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рддрд╛рдГред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдордкреАрддреНрдпреБрдкрдзрд╛рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН) (рджреЗрд╡реАрдГ) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпреЗрди (рд╕рдиреЗрдо) рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрднреНрдпреЛ рджрджреНрдпрд╛рдо (рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд┐рдгрдореН) рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдорд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╛ рдЧреБрдгрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрдореН (рдЪ) (рд╢рддрд┐рдирдореН) рд╢рддрд╢реЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдЪ) (рд╡рд╛рдЬрдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдордпрдВ рдмреЛрдзрдореН рее резрей рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬрд╢реА рдЙрд╖рд╛ рд╢реБрдн рдЧреБрдг, рдХрд░реНрдо, рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЕрд╕рддреЗ. рддрд╢реА рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡реА. рддрд╢реАрдЪ рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗрд╣реА рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡реАрдд. рдЬрд╕реЗ рдЗрддрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдХрдбреВрди рдЖрдкрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЬрдирд╛рд╕рд╛рдареА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдШреЗрддреЛ рддрд╢реА рдкреНрд░реЗрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдЗрддрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛рд╣реА рддреА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реА. рее резрей рее
